SCENE TITLE: WHAT SLIPS UNDER DOORS
The rain thickens, sound flattening the world beyond the glass. The inn settles again—wood creaking as if relieved you haven’t
moved yet. Whatever slid under your door waits without impatience. Paper doesn’t breathe. People do.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🦊 JAYSON | 🕯️🦊
📝 You look at the paper for a long time, then get up to take it and read it.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The parchment is coarse, cheap—market stock. Folded once. No seal. No guild mark. No scent of oil or wax.
Just ink.
The handwriting is tight and deliberate, pressed hard enough to scar the fibers.
> “You are being watched by three eyes, not two.
> 
> The one closest to you is not the most dangerous.
> 
> Do not leave the inn tonight.
> 
> If she asks about the lights—lie.”
At the bottom, a mark instead of a name.
A simple symbol, scratched rather than drawn:
a broken circle, split clean through one side.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🎲 RANDOM TURN | TENSION [⚖️]
From the corridor—soft footsteps pause. Someone lingers, breath held just long enough to be deliberate… then continues past your
door.
Whoever sent the message didn’t wait to see if you read it.

SCENE TITLE: WHERE THE RAIN STANDS STILL
The door sighs shut behind you and the city takes you back. Rain beads on your cloak, cold and honest. River Ward stretches narrow
here—stone pressed close, gutters running fast, lanterns blurred into halos that bleed into puddles.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🦊 JAYSON | 🌧️👁️
📝 You step out into the street and look for the one who stopped under your window.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No one stands directly beneath it now.
Just aftermath.
A puddle still shivers, disturbed seconds too late. A bootprint darkens the grit—weight held, then released. Whoever waited didn’t
linger long enough to be seen, only long enough to be known.
Across the lane, a fishmonger’s awning snaps in the wind. Beyond it, three figures move through rain at different depths of the
street:
 * 
   One walks openly, hood down, unconcerned.
 * 
   One keeps to cover, pace matching yours without turning.
 * 
   One is only a reflection—present in the glass of a shuttered shop, gone when you look twice.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🎲 RANDOM TURN | CONVERGENCE [⚖️👁️]
A cart rattles past, momentarily breaking lines of sight.
When it clears, the reflection is closer.
Not hostile.
Not friendly.
Just… attentive.
The city exhales, as if waiting to see which way you’ll go.

gathered.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The openly walking figure slows first—then stops, turning just enough for lamplight to catch a familiar profile.
Kestrel.
She’s not armored. No guild colors. Just travel leathers darkened by rain, hair damp at the edges. Her eyes flick once—past you,
not to you—counting something you can’t see.
The second presence peels away into an alley without sound. The third never steps out at all; the reflection thins, stretches, and
breaks across a windowpane as if the glass itself chose to forget it.

🍶 "HARROWFEN — RIVER WARD INN, COMMON HALL (CORNER TABLE)" | 🌧️ "RAIN (POURING)" | 🌙 "EVENING, 18:31" | 📅 "18/04/1427"
SCENE TITLE: WHEN STILLNESS GETS LOUD
It is like something out of an anime—time stretched thin while the world cycles.
People come.
People go.
Beastfolk slip in with hoods tight and shoulders hunched, eyes down, meals eaten fast and paid for faster. A pair of wolfkin share
a bowl, backs to the wall, gone before the steam fades. A catfolk courier darts in, grabs bread, vanishes like they were never
meant to be seen.

Or notice and choose not to.

And that’s the problem.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Silence is normal here—
for a moment.
For a breath.
But sustained silence?
That starts to glow.
Laughter surges. Dice slam. Someone spills a drink and swears creatively. And yet—your corner doesn’t change. You don’t shout.
Don’t boast. Don’t complain. You just observe.
Eventually, the contrast becomes impossible to ignore.
A young adventurer at a nearby table squints your way, elbowing his friend.

> 💬 "The one not doing anything?"
> 
> 💬 "Yeah. That’s weird."
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Near the bar, a veteran notices too—not by looking directly at you, but by noting who isn’t moving. Her mug pauses halfway to her
lips. She shifts her seat subtly, giving herself a better angle on the room.
The bard’s eyes flick your way between verses.
Even the innkeep clocks it—just a fraction of a second longer than necessary as he wipes the counter.
Still no confrontation.
Still no alarm.
Just awareness spreading like ripples.

> 💬 "Oi."
> 
> 💬 "You been sittin’ there all night, friend."
A pause. Not hostile.
Just loud enough that nearby conversations soften, not stop—but bend toward you.
The inn doesn’t fall silent.
But for the first time tonight—
The noise is waiting to see if you will make some of it.

SCENE TITLE: FLOATING, AT LAST
Hooks creak softly as you hang your coat and clothes—no rush, no hesitation. Steam curls around stone pillars, carrying the low
murmur of conversation and the steady splash of water against tile.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🦊 JAYSON | SHAMELESS-RELIEF [🦊🛁]
📝 You pad to the pool’s edge, take one look at the inviting surface—
—and belly flop in.
Water erupts in a friendly, unbothered splash. A few ripples of laughter answer from elsewhere in the bath, nothing sharp, nothing
judging.
📝 You surface, then let yourself go slack, floating on your back like a dead body—ears just above the surface, tails spreading
and buoyant, limbs loose, eyes half-lidded.
The water holds you.
No gravity to fight.
No blade to shape.
No room to read.
Just heat and buoyancy doing honest work.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🧭 KESTREL | AMUSED-ACCEPTING [⚔️😌]
From the steps, she watches you drift, a corner of her mouth lifting.
> 💬 "Subtle."
She eases into the pool a moment later, keeping a respectful distance, letting the steam do its thing.
> 💬 "You look like you finally remembered how to float."
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
🎲 RANDOM TURN | CALM-CLAIMED [🌫️]
The bathhouse settles around you—water sloshing, stone warm, time losing its sharp edges. For a few precious minutes, the world
asks nothing of you.
You float.
And nothing pulls you under.
